<span id="freeTextContainer17240397727036060041">Teen angst has never been such serious business - or this much fun! In his secret diary, British teen Adrian Mole excruciatingly details every morsel of his turbulent adolescence. Mixed in with daily reports about the spot sprouting on his chin are heartrending passages about his parents' chaotic marriage.<br /><br />Adrian sees all, and he has something to say about everything. Delig</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17240397727036060041">Teen angst has never been such serious business - or this much fun! In his secret diary, British teen Adrian Mole excruciatingly details every morsel of his turbulent adolescence. Mixed in with daily reports about the spot sprouting on his chin are heartrending passages about his parents' chaotic marriage.<br /><br />Adrian sees all, and he has something to say about everything. Delightfully self-centered, Adrian is the sort of teen who could rule a much better world - if only his crazy relatives and classmates would get out of his way!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_318591838">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/318591838" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1713956-manny" class="left imgcol" title="Manny"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442491692p2/1713956.jpg" alt="Manny" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/318591838?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 25, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1713956-manny" class="user" title="Manny">Manny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/51070.The_Secret_Diary_of_Adrian_Mole_Aged_13_3_4" title="Paperback 9780060533991" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=children" class="actionLinkLite">children</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=well-i-think-its-funny" class="actionLinkLite">well-i-think-its-funny</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=parody-homage" class="actionLinkLite">parody-homage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer318591838">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12710286595144418730"><strong>April 25</strong><br /><br />I start reading a book called <em>Diary of a Nobody</em>. It is boring and not much happens, also Mr. Pooter is pretty dim. I don't get it. Why would anyone want to write a book about a nobody who takes himself far too seriously? <br /><br />I decide that I will write a book about myself that will be quite different, it will be full of important things I do and extremely interesting. Perhaps I will call it <em>Diary of a Somebody</em>. But then people won't know which somebody it is, since everyone is somebody. I dec</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12710286595144418730"><strong>April 25</strong><br /><br />I start reading a book called <em>Diary of a Nobody</em>. It is boring and not much happens, also Mr. Pooter is pretty dim. I don't get it. Why would anyone want to write a book about a nobody who takes himself far too seriously? <br /><br />I decide that I will write a book about myself that will be quite different, it will be full of important things I do and extremely interesting. Perhaps I will call it <em>Diary of a Somebody</em>. But then people won't know which somebody it is, since everyone is somebody. I decide that a better title will be <em>Secret Diary of Adrian Mole Aged 13 and 3/4</em>. I am just about to start writing some important things when my mother reminds me that I said I would tidy up my room. I will write about them when I have finished tidying.<br /><br /><strong>April 26</strong><br /><br />I have received letters from two people I don't know, called MJ Nicholls and Knig-o-lass. They both want to be in my diary. This is a bit strange, since my diary is secret, but I write back to say I will put them in if they do some silly things with yoga, teddy bears and toffee apples. I think this is very original, and shows I am a Somebody. <br /><br /><strong>April 27</strong><br /><br />I have received another letter from MJ. He says he wants his own days in my diary, so I will not mention anyone else today. I had not understood that keeping a diary was so complicated. <br /><br /><strong>April 28</strong><br /><br />I am trying to imagine what Miss Knig-o-lass looks like. I see her as a beautiful, treacle-haired temptress, like Pandora at school. I am hoping that she will also send me a request. <br /><br />Miss Knig-o-lass does not seem as demanding as MJ. Perhaps this is because she is a nicer person, or perhaps it is just because she hasn't noticed me. It's often hard to tell with girls.<br /><br /><strong>April 29</strong><br /><br />Miss Knig-o-lass has also sent me a request! I don't really understand it, but there is a card with a stretched-out picture of a lady and something about how chocolate can't get you pregnant. I must make sure that Pandora does not find out about my friendship with this sophisticated older woman.<br /><br /><strong>April 30</strong><br /><br />MJ has sent me another message! He says he might be jealous. I think he must be Miss Knig-o-lass's regular boyfriend. He used a Latin word I didn't know, I wish I had been paying more attention in biology yesterday when we were doing Human Reproduction. <br /><br />Since I started keeping this diary my life has become more and more interesting. I am definitely a Somebody.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12710286595144418730">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16935350927792741807">Thank you for drawing my attention to one Adrian Mole -- although, as a teacher, I fear I have seen too many Adrian Moles in my life. Also, <a title="The Diary of a Nobody by George Grossmith" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/535856.The_Diary_of_a_Nobody">The Diary of a Nobody</a> is a lot funnier in audio format. <span id="freeTextContainer8646256662917285453">This book is a hoot. I used to read it on the train and had to stop doing so because people around me were annoyed by my laughing and snorting. <br /><br />I don't know how Townsend knows so much about the workings of a male teenaged mind, but it's thoroughly convincing and all hilarious.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText8646256662917285453">This book is a hoot. I used to read it on the train and had to stop doing so because people around me were annoyed by my laughing and snorting. <br /><br />I don't know how Townsend knows so much about the workings of a male teenaged mind, but it's thoroughly convincing and all hilarious. Adrian Mole is a young intellectual and poet, constantly disgusted by his un-intellectual parents whose marriage is rocky and who split up during the course of the novel. Mole spends a lot of time agonising over his age (especially his acne) and submitting heartfelt poems to the BBC to be published. Mole delights with his honest descriptions and experiences with puberty, pornography, masturbation, school bullying, volunteer work with the elderly and his first love, the beautiful school prefect, Pandora. <br /><br />Untitled (Monday, 28 September -- Secret Diary)<br /><br />Bert, you are dead old.<br />Fond of Sabre, beetroot and Woodbines.<br />We have nothing in common,<br />I am fourteen and a half,<br />You are eighty-nine.<br />You smell, I don't.<br />Why we are friends<br />Is a mystery to me.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer207789192320577025">The Diary of Adrian Mole is like a snarky one-liner that continues for 135 pages. She told Claire Neilson, who told Nigel, who told me.</em><br /><br /><em>I told Nigel to tell Claire to tell Pandora that I return her love. I am over the moon with joy and rapture. I can overlook the fact that Pandora smokes five Benson and Hedges a day and has her own lighter. Whe</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText207789192320577025">The Diary of Adrian Mole is like a snarky one-liner that continues for 135 pages. Adrian is a self-centered, irreverent British 14-year-old whose diary entries include nuggets of wisdom such as:<br /><br /><em>Pandora and I are in love! It is official! She told Claire Neilson, who told Nigel, who told me.</em><br /><br /><em>I told Nigel to tell Claire to tell Pandora that I return her love. I am over the moon with joy and rapture. I can overlook the fact that Pandora smokes five Benson and Hedges a day and has her own lighter. When you are in love such things cease to matter.</em><br /><br />It was entertaining, but never really got beyond the point of a quick, light read.<br /><br />I did learn that there was a short-lived BBC series based on the book.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer335990518">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18389630157609082073">I've just read this to my daughter who is exactly this age. I'd read the book when it first came out but it was great to revisit both it and the memories that it stirred. Reliving the Falklands War, the Royal Wedding, mass unemployment, stress over the changes to the school system etc was fascinating if only to realise how little has changed! We almost had to stop reading at one point as each day's literary Mole catastrophe coincidentally seemed to then occur in my daughter's real life: her firs</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18389630157609082073">I've just read this to my daughter who is exactly this age. I'd read the book when it first came out but it was great to revisit both it and the memories that it stirred. Reliving the Falklands War, the Royal Wedding, mass unemployment, stress over the changes to the school system etc was fascinating if only to realise how little has changed! We almost had to stop reading at one point as each day's literary Mole catastrophe coincidentally seemed to then occur in my daughter's real life: her first spot, the disastrous school trip...! We both loved it and she has been inspired to start a diary! I've read everyone of the Mole books - the Weapons of Mass Destruction will remain my favourite for obvious reasons! What a talent. Word of warning though: if you do get these on audio books, don't play them in the car while driving. I came close to crashing when one anecdote in The Capuccino Years blinded me with tears of hysterical laughter just outside Colchester. I had to stop the car to recover and compose myself with a hefty dose of R4 Woman's Hour instead.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18389630157609082073">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/289692602?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8073293-tim-roast" class="user" title="Tim Roast">Tim Roast</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7742547-the-secret-diary-of-adrian-mole-aged-13" title="Paperback 9780141046426" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer289692602">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13028384484791399279">You've probably heard of "The Secret (although not anymore it would seem) Diary of Adrian Mole Aged 13 " but I'll review it anyway.<br /><br />The diary covers the period January 1981 through to beginning of April 1982. Therefore Adrian was not 13  throughout the story (false advertising?); instead he was merely 13  at the beginning and 15 at the end.<br /><br />It is now 30 years since the diary's release and apart from mentions to the price of things (30,000 for a semi-detached house, if only) and the mention of cert</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13028384484791399279">You've probably heard of "The Secret (although not anymore it would seem) Diary of Adrian Mole Aged 13 ¾" but I'll review it anyway.<br /><br />The diary covers the period January 1981 through to beginning of April 1982. Therefore Adrian was not 13 ¾ throughout the story (false advertising?); instead he was merely 13 ¾ at the beginning and 15 at the end.<br /><br />It is now 30 years since the diary's release and apart from mentions to the price of things (£30,000 for a semi-detached house, if only) and the mention of certain politicians of the time it hasn't really dated. Big events of the time are covered like the Royal wedding between Prince Charles and Lady Diana. Also the country is in a recession it seems which may have reflected the time period (I was born during the time period so can't remember it but have been told that it was a recession).<br /><br />Adrian Mole is funny because of his "woe is me" attitude to everything that happens to him. He is an intellectual too (self-classified). He also has an innocence, particularly at the beginning of the book, to what goes on around him that leads to some more funny moments.<br /><br />All in all I think this book has already proved itself what with its many millions of sales. If I were to say it were rubbish then it wouldn't matter, but I liked it and thoroughly recommend it to people after a laugh.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13028384484791399279">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_431936841">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/431936841" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10917030-amanda" class="left imgcol" title="Amanda"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1351197916p2/10917030.jpg" alt="Amanda" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/431936841?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 01, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10917030-amanda" class="user" title="Amanda">Amanda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/51070.The_Secret_Diary_of_Adrian_Mole_Aged_13_3_4" title="Paperback 9780060533991" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Harry Potter (in case he needs another book to stab)</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Amanda by: </span>
      It was forced on me! I will deny every argument against this!
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10917030-amanda?shelf=books-i-hated" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-hated</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10917030-amanda?shelf=reviewed-books" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10917030-amanda?shelf=school-assigned" class="actionLinkLite">school-assigned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/10917030-amanda?shelf=im-about-to-die-of-boredom" class="actionLinkLite">im-about-to-die-of-boredom</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer431936841">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10347809899513700051"><strong>1 dead star.</strong><br />Yes, I hate this book so much, I killed its sole, lonely star. <br /><br />As this was a school assigned book, I have written a much more formal review from an objective point of view for my English class. I also wrote a review purely for me, from a very subjective point of view. Feel free to just read the objective one but if you want to see how bad the book was for me, personally, read to the end.<br />Without further ado...<br /><br /><u>The Objective Review:</u><br />From an objective point of view, The Secret Diary of Ad</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10347809899513700051"><strong>1 dead star.</strong><br />Yes, I hate this book so much, I killed its sole, lonely star. <br /><br />As this was a school assigned book, I have written a much more formal review from an objective point of view for my English class. I also wrote a review purely for me, from a very subjective point of view. Feel free to just read the objective one but if you want to see how bad the book was for me, personally, read to the end.<br />Without further ado...<br /><br /><u>The Objective Review:</u><br />From an objective point of view, The Secret Diary of Adrian Mole Aged 13 ¾ wasn’t half bad. <br /><br />Adrian Mole is your average, English, teenage boy living in the 80’s. As he goes through puberty, he must struggle with conflicting emotions, parent troubles, pimples, and first love. I would have preferred the diary to be on a more interesting character and lifestyle but that is just my personal preference.<br /><br />This book is told from Adrian Mole’s point of view, in a series of diary entries. The mundane, everyday updates could provide many points for the reader to relate to. <br /><br />Adrian is, quite frankly, an ungrateful, arrogant kid, but in the underlying messages, you can tell he does have an understanding of love. The things his family goes through would be pretty tough for a teenager who also has his own internal problems. I did not like him very much, as some of the things he said were pretty insulting. Teenage boys will probably find traits they can relate to, but, as I am a girl, I did not find any.<br /><br />The supporting characters include Pandora, Adrian’s love interest, Adrian’s father, mother, grandmother, and an old man name Bert Baxter. He had one of the more interesting stories but he was not a main focus of the novel.<br /><br />The plot was not very well done. I understand that it is meant to have a very natural, raw feel to it, being a diary of a teenage boy, but I felt that it was very random and disjointed. The events had no order to them, which I find really annoying as I like things to be organized. There was no climax, even in the background themes. It was a sequence of mundane events with no big event to tie everything together. The ending was so abrupt, I thought the author just wrote the whole book series at once, and told the publisher to chop it wherever they needed to make them into perfectly identical books. <br />There was also very minimal character development. Adrian has the same personality at the end as he has at the start. <br /><br />The writing style was also very jerky. As it is from Adrian’s hand, it is explainable. I just did not like it. I have always been a fan of the fluent, lyrical, poetic prose, so this amateurish, jerky writing was not to my taste.<br /><br />In the visual department, the cover is very boring. There is nothing to really suggest the story or Adrian’s personality. The formatting of the text inside the book is rather squashed together as most old books are. There are drawings inserted on random pages in the book but I didn’t pay much attention to them. I assume they represent certain events in the story.<br /><br />In the 80’s this book would have been as popular as Diary of a Wimpy Kid is today. But as I was clearly out of the target demographic, I did not like this book very much. Actually, not at all.<br /><br /><br /><u>The Subjective Review:</u><br />I regret choosing this for Literature Circles. If anyone asks, it was forced on me. See my status updates for my emotions while reading.<br /><br />Multiple Choice Question:<br />Is Adrian Mole:<br />A: sexist<br />B: ungrateful<br />C: an insult to fourteen year olds<br />D: not an intellectual<br />TRICK QUESTION! He is in fact, answer E: all of the above AND THEN SOME!<br /><br />I don't know where to start explaining this horrible excuse for a fourteen year old. He calls himself an intellectual, yet his poems sound like <a title="City of Bones (The Mortal Instruments, #1) by Cassandra Clare" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/256683.City_of_Bones__The_Mortal_Instruments___1_">"he ate a dictionary and started vomiting up words at random."</a> He spends the whole book whinging, whining, groaning, moaning, and complaining about every little thing that goes wrong in his life. <br />*puts on cutesy kindergarten teacher voice* Okay, children. Today I am going to tell you the meaning of life. It's not perfect, and it's damn hard. If you wanted the easy way out, you should have been born dead instead. Living is hard. Do we all understand that? *cough*Adrian Mole*cough*<br /><br />Approaching his caricature from an impersonal, critical, analytical view (like my English teacher said), I can see how this would appeal to teenage boys...back in the 80's. Yeah, I bet that back then it was as popular as <a title="Diary of a Wimpy Kid (Diary of a Wimpy Kid, #1) by Jeff Kinney" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/389627.Diary_of_a_Wimpy_Kid__Diary_of_a_Wimpy_Kid___1_">Diary of a Wimpy Kid</a>. But today? A snowflake's chance on the sun. <br /><br />"Pandora<br />I adore ya<br />I implore ye<br />Don't ignore me." <br />Can anyone say INSTA-LOVE? <br /><br />Now, moving onto plot since the supporting characters were so uninteresting...oh wait...hang on...I don't seem to be detecting a plot anywhere within these 187 pages. Oh dear. Well to sum it up, he made New Years resolutions, he measured his 'thing', read indecent magazines, hid the phone bill, his parents split up, his dog went missing, he caters for this old guy who ends up in hospital then gets married, falls in love with Pandora, goes to Derbyshire, and shaves. Not in that order. I also do not understand how it ended. Just couldn't end at the end of 1982 couldn't you? You just had to throw in three months of 1983 and cut it off in the most random place possible? For Lit Circles, we had do this Narrative summary thing where you use that story mountain to identify the parts of the story. When we got up to the part where we were supposed to write the climax, there was a collective silence. THERE IS NO CLIMAX. All rising action that shouldn't be called rising action because it doesn't build up to anything!<br /><br />The writing is so jerky, the book should be a piece of beef. Again with the analytical approach: it fits the story and Adrian's caricature. But for the reader who happens to HATE poorly written books? No.<br /><br />What I really don't understand is why the book is written about a boring, ordinary guy who has nothing happening in his life. From the impersonal approach, I can see the author tried to appeal to the ordinary teenager back in the 80's. But aren't books fiction for a reason? Don't you write and read them to experience the things that would never happen in your own life? In my opinion, a diary should be from the point of view of a person who has had something memorable happen in their life. Like say, <a title="The Diary of a Young Girl by Anne Frank" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/48855.The_Diary_of_a_Young_Girl">Anne Frank?</a><br /><br />I am seriously considering stabbing this book like Harry Potter stabbed Tom Riddle's diary. I don't care that it's school property. Give me a Basilisk fang, phone charger, umbrella, plastic spork, I'm not fussed, and I'll stab it and relish in the way the ink bleeds off the pages into oblivion.<br /><img width="300" height="225" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380393967r/758531._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />No, seriously. I need that Basilisk fang.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10347809899513700051">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer12219535249644411419">I have been meaning to read this classic for YEARS.<br /><br />Poor old Adrian: so innocent and pompous and self-deluded, all at the same time. This book is very, very English; I think that I had just enough knowledge of the culture (after 24 years of being with a British man) to pretty much "get" it. It also helps that I was more or less the same age as Adrian in the early 1980s. Great social document, with some enduring humour -- a lot of it in the gap between what Adrian thinks/understands and what the r</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12219535249644411419">I have been meaning to read this classic for YEARS.<br /><br />Poor old Adrian: so innocent and pompous and self-deluded, all at the same time. This book is very, very English; I think that I had just enough knowledge of the culture (after 24 years of being with a British man) to pretty much "get" it. It also helps that I was more or less the same age as Adrian in the early 1980s. Great social document, with some enduring humour -- a lot of it in the gap between what Adrian thinks/understands and what the reader understands. Although most of the humour holds up, some of the details of school/home life/politics will seem foreignly "historical" to a contemporary teenager. I don't know if I love it enough to follow the entire series, but I've had Adrian Mole: The Cappuccino Years on my TBR shelf for ages . . . so definitely that one at least. By the way, my edition has a great foreword from David Walliams -- definitely worth a read, if you are the sort of person to skip that kind of thing.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16581681832742799802">Adrian, how is it that we've only just met? You're hilarious. I laughed so frequently that my husband took you from my possession as soon as I was finished and started reading as well. The title of the final book is ADRIAN MOLE: THE PROSTRATE YEARS.<br /><br />Thank you Jen! This little copy traveled home with me from London and I can't think of a better souvenir.<br /><br />The author also has a non-fiction book called PUBLIC CONFESSIONS OF A MIDDLE AGED WOMAN AGED 55-3/4. I've read it so many times (the edition whose cover is an homage to "Catcher in the Rye") my original copy is worn. Luckily, I was able to get my own copy soon and absolutely fell in love with Adrian. <br />Most of the sequels are just as good (especially the Cappuccino Years), but it could be just because Sue Townsend writes for my generation, though she is not quite of it. I had a chance to meet her when I was working at BPL but couldn't because of work. I wanted desperately to meet her as I envisioned her as the mother of what I occasionaly felt as my literary husband, dork though he was.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12948847756042874094">Bought this at the EuroStar train station in London. Had never heard of it, seemed like sort of an English Judy Blume. I have multiple times laughed out loud.<br />Very enjoyable overall. In the world of authors, Sue Townsend is in a neighboring cul-da-sac from Roald Dahl. Quirky character names, a lead who hasn't got the best of luck but you still root for, a dirty, wry sense of humor and a touch of English. Poor Adrian Mole's parents are breaking apart, no one can control the family's nameless dog,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12948847756042874094">Bought this at the EuroStar train station in London. Had never heard of it, seemed like sort of an English Judy Blume. I have multiple times laughed out loud.<br />Very enjoyable overall. In the world of authors, Sue Townsend is in a neighboring cul-da-sac from Roald Dahl. Quirky character names, a lead who hasn't got the best of luck but you still root for, a dirty, wry sense of humor and a touch of English. Poor Adrian Mole's parents are breaking apart, no one can control the family's nameless dog, he's recently become the companion of the elderly (and surly) Bert Baxter and he's desperately in love with Pandora but she's dating his friend. Adrian's voice is unique and observant, and even as an adult I laughed aloud more than once. The series brought Adrian into adulthood, with the most recent published only a few years back. I'm not sure that I'll read the entire series, but I really enjoyed getting to know Adrian and his attitude. If you have some free time by the pool this summer, this one will keep you laughing.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_706440644">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/706440644" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/23284117-simon-taylor" class="left imgcol" title="Simon Taylor"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442951658p2/23284117.jpg" alt="Simon Taylor" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/706440644?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 29, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/23284117-simon-taylor" class="user" title="Simon Taylor">Simon Taylor</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/51070.The_Secret_Diary_of_Adrian_Mole_Aged_13_3_4" title="Paperback 9780060533991" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer706440644">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6411730474334011716">Like other things for the 13’s like Haribo and cheesy films, they can be enjoyed by adults and children alike. On the surface, Adrian lives an entertaining life, caught up in the dramas of the day-to-day: school, family, girls and a horribly tight budget. We can relate to his experiences, both trials and triumphs, and easily engage with the titular calendar. Sue Townsend does a brilliant job of regressing to her teenage years to remember the intimacies of the most awkward age group.<br /><br />For the adult</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6411730474334011716">Like other things for the 13¾’s like Haribo and cheesy films, they can be enjoyed by adults and children alike. On the surface, Adrian lives an entertaining life, caught up in the dramas of the day-to-day: school, family, girls and a horribly tight budget. We can relate to his experiences, both trials and triumphs, and easily engage with the titular calendar. Sue Townsend does a brilliant job of regressing to her teenage years to remember the intimacies of the most awkward age group.<br /><br />For the adult reader, though, Adrian Mole represents more than daft fun. While his peers will share in his bewilderment, Townsend cleverly gives just enough clues to her more mature audience to piece the jigsaw together and read between the lines. Also set firmly in 1982—1983, Margaret Thatcher’s government has an important role to play. The political sympathies of the characters’ are alluded to and often stated explicitly, along with the bias and preconceptions Adrian has picked up from his parents.<br /><br />Mole, 13¾ – and the series in general – has a really clever element of social commentary, mapping the attitudes and sympathies of the British public throughout real events, such as the wedding of Charles and Diana in this first instalment. This takes the series from being disposable fun to a shrewd, carefully considered archive of public feeling.<br /><br />Townsend’s decision to present the story as a diary, as the title would suggest, gives us a unique insight into Adrian’s mind. There are some genuine laugh-out-loud moments that just invoke hysteria, with Adrian’s experiences, perceptions and rapidly changing views. The writing is short and snappy and keeps the pace going and it impressively doesn’t miss a single date in over a year, besides the brief couple of days he left his diary at home. Written from Adrian’s viewpoint entirely, the self-absorbed teenaged attitude provides a refreshingly fun alternative to the adult narrator you’d expect with their levelled understanding, and is a perfect vehicle to the social commentary and exposure of prejudices. Although it does, arguably, limit how well you can get to know the other characters, Townsend does a magnificent job of building a really vivid, colourful cast through Adrian’s eyes that doesn’t leave you cheated at all.<br /><br />A fantastic read that’s nostalgic (without a rose tint) for not just the 1980’s, but also the 13¾’s.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6411730474334011716">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer7189225041206306899">I have read this book for school, well, an adaptation of it. What can I say? This story is about a boy that writes on his diary all his adventures and actions during the day. It was really funny, firstly because it's not the kind of books I usually read for classes, this surprised me. A lot. <br />I couldn't laugh more with Adrian's worries about spots, it's the first boy I know (even it's fictional) that cares about that! <br />He's in love with Pandora, a girl that, personally thinking, is a girl that bri</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7189225041206306899">I have read this book for school, well, an adaptation of it. What can I say? This story is about a boy that writes on his diary all his adventures and actions during the day. It was really funny, firstly because it's not the kind of books I usually read for classes, this surprised me. A lot. <br />I couldn't laugh more with Adrian's worries about spots, it's the first boy I know (even it's fictional) that cares about that! <br />He's in love with Pandora, a girl that, personally thinking, is a girl that brings closer to who she thinks it will make her life easier, by the way, as a book with "happy ending", she notices that Adrian is the good one, the boy that'll make her heart go wow. <br />This book tells us so many things, not like other books about teenage boys, for example the changes on his body, his reaction to see a naked girl, etc. <br />I recommend everyone to read this book and, I think I'll read the extended story one day!</span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of pompous young men and British humor</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/142816-heavyreader?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer265232647">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8735594610466575793">Adrian Mole is a pompous, self-centered, arrogant little snot.<br /><br />What is up with these 14 year old boy books where the boy is all about himself from beginning to end? Did Ponyboy spoil me forever? Ponyboy, now there's a nice, sensitive kid. <br /><br />The worst part of this book (like others of this genre that I've read recently) is that I just don't see much character development. This character is pretty much the same, beginning to end.<br /><br />I did laugh out loud in a couple of spots, and that's what saved this bo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8735594610466575793">Adrian Mole is a pompous, self-centered, arrogant little snot.<br /><br />What is up with these 14 year old boy books where the boy is all about himself from beginning to end? Did Ponyboy spoil me forever? Ponyboy, now there's a nice, sensitive kid. <br /><br />The worst part of this book (like others of this genre that I've read recently) is that I just don't see much character development. This character is pretty much the same, beginning to end.<br /><br />I did laugh out loud in a couple of spots, and that's what saved this book from getting one star.<br /><br />I wanted to like this book. I really did. Unfortunately, I just didn't like it much at all.<br /><br />(My problem may be that I just don't understand British humor.)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_865410042">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/865410042" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5810205-james" class="left imgcol" title="James"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442598732p2/5810205.jpg" alt="James" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/865410042?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 29, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5810205-james" class="user" title="James">James</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/51070.The_Secret_Diary_of_Adrian_Mole_Aged_13_3_4" title="Paperback 9780060533991" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer865410042">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16731396479318792189">Adrian Mole is a self-proclaimed intellectual, growing up in 1980s England. His mother runs off with the neighbor and his father loses his job and does little to support Adrian, who is often left to fend for himself. This book is his diary of 1 1/2 years, and it is dead hilarious (to put it like Adrian might). I'm not sure how this one passed me by when I was a teen in the '80s. I didn't have all of the same problems as Adrian, but I could definitely have related to him.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer35509459">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7377718005099888589">Adrian Mole is a 13-year-old self-styled intellectual who is 'at the same time not very clever.' I love the way he pesters the BBC with unsolicited poetry, and treasures his rejection letters. He's definitely the young fogey in his family, often aligning himself with his grandmother against his adulterous mother and unemployed father. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a href="/book/show/18816993-the-secret-diary-of-adrian-mole-aged-13-3-4" title="Kindle Edition 9780718196134" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1412368788">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6364221204153612747">Elegido para el Club de Lectura por Lum.<br />No pude entrar en sintonía con este libro. Adrian Mole, me pareció un personaje superficial, idiota y desagradable (por solo nombrar algunas de sus cualidades horribles). Sus actitudes egoístas y su incapacidad de amar me repugnaron. Si la autora pensó que estaba siendo graciosa cuando lo escribía, subestimó mucho a sus lectores, en las 200 páginas del libro no me sacó ni una mínima sonrisa. Prácticamente leí todo el libro con el ceño fruncido.<br />Tampoco me p</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6364221204153612747">Elegido para el Club de Lectura por Lum.<br />No pude entrar en sintonía con este libro. Adrian Mole, me pareció un personaje superficial, idiota y desagradable (por solo nombrar algunas de sus cualidades horribles). Sus actitudes egoístas y su incapacidad de amar me repugnaron. Si la autora pensó que estaba siendo graciosa cuando lo escribía, subestimó mucho a sus lectores, en las 200 páginas del libro no me sacó ni una mínima sonrisa. Prácticamente leí todo el libro con el ceño fruncido.<br />Tampoco me pareció que retratara correctamente a un niño de 13 años, por momentos parece de 6 y por otros un adulto. Así que ni ahí le pagó.<br />Lo único positivo es que es corto y como está escrito de forma muy boluda se lee bastante rápido, gracias a Dios! Estoy feliz por haberlo terminado y saber que nunca más voy a leer nada relacionado a este personaje o autora! xD</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6364221204153612747">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4263944607736182880">With the recent death of Sue Townsend I decided to re-read Adrian Mole only to discover my previous copy was falling apart at the spine. I read the series once every few years and realising that they will never be another is a great disappointed as he is a character I have followed through his "life". I read this for the first time when I was 12/13 and like everyone else since publication identified with Adrian Mole. The fact that a 30 year old woman can write about a teenage boy so perfectly on</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4263944607736182880">With the recent death of Sue Townsend I decided to re-read Adrian Mole only to discover my previous copy was falling apart at the spine. I read the series once every few years and realising that they will never be another is a great disappointed as he is a character I have followed through his "life". I read this for the first time when I was 12/13 and like everyone else since publication identified with Adrian Mole. The fact that a 30 year old woman can write about a teenage boy so perfectly only shows what an amazing writer Townsend was and what a loss her death was.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_772403573">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/772403573" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2298519-mizannie" class="left imgcol" title="Mizannie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1344817304p2/2298519.jpg" alt="Mizannie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/772403573?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2298519-mizannie" class="user" title="Mizannie">Mizannie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/51070.The_Secret_Diary_of_Adrian_Mole_Aged_13_3_4" title="Paperback 9780060533991" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer772403573">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3303355968239565300">Sue Townsend had a knack for capturing the inner life of the adolescent boy. We meet Adrian Mole via his diary entries and through them learn of his insecurities, his abysmal home life, and his big heart. Adrian is a self-proclaimed "intellectual" and his diary entry lists what he is reading, although his school grades are certainly not spectacular. Socially awkward, Adrian navigates a crush on a pretty girl with "treacle hair," deals with a school bully, and volunteers to visit an elderly perso</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3303355968239565300">Sue Townsend had a knack for capturing the inner life of the adolescent boy. We meet Adrian Mole via his diary entries and through them learn of his insecurities, his abysmal home life, and his big heart. Adrian is a self-proclaimed "intellectual" and his diary entry lists what he is reading, although his school grades are certainly not spectacular. Socially awkward, Adrian navigates a crush on a pretty girl with "treacle hair," deals with a school bully, and volunteers to visit an elderly person. While some have criticized this character as a "self-absorbed snot," I would remind folks that developmentally speaking this character is spot-on (no pun intended to Adrian's complexion problems) in terms of viewing the world in a somewhat narcissistic way. Like all adolescents Adrian is outgrowing childhood and wanting to be taken care of (and his somatic complaints are often the only way to get nurturance from his parents, who are wrapped up in their own marital issues). At the same time, he wants to experience love, get his first job, and has dreams of becoming a famous writer and/or veterinarian. Completely normal, in other words, as he transitions from child to teenager. Quirky and charming.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3303355968239565300">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer197562281">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9859739075445035745">This is the hilarious deadpan diary of Adrian Mole. He’s 13 and , his mother is having an affair with the next door neighbor, whose wife has left him for another woman. His father is having a nervous breakdown and has lost his job, and Adrian is pining for the lovely Pandora who is dating his best friend Nigel. Adrian decides that he is a poet and an intellectual, and yet sometimes he just fails to see things as they are. His innocence and naïvete are hysterical. <br /><br />Excerpt:<br /><br />Thursday March 12th<br /><br />Woke</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9859739075445035745">This is the hilarious deadpan diary of Adrian Mole. He’s 13 and ¾, his mother is having an affair with the next door neighbor, whose wife has left him for another woman. His father is having a nervous breakdown and has lost his job, and Adrian is pining for the lovely Pandora who is dating his best friend Nigel. Adrian decides that he is a poet and an intellectual, and yet sometimes he just fails to see things as they are. His innocence and naïvete are hysterical. <br /><br />Excerpt:<br /><br />Thursday March 12th<br /><br />Woke up this morning to find my face covered in huge red spots. My mother said they were caused by nerves but I am still convinced that my diet is inadequate. We had been eating a lot of boil-in-the-bag stuff lately. Perhaps I am allergic to plastic. My mother rang Dr. Gray’s receptionist to make an appointment, but the earliest he can see me is next Monday! For all he knows I could have lassa fever and be spreading it all around the district! I told my mother to say that I was an emergency case but she said I was ‘overreacting as usual.’ She said a few spots didn’t mean I was dying. I couldn’t believe it when she said she was going to work as usual. Surely her child should come before her job? <br />	I rang my grandma and she came round in a taxi and took me to her house and put me to bed. I am there now. It is very clean and peaceful. I am wearing my dead grandad’s pyjamas. I have just had a bowl of barley and beef soup. It is my first proper nourishment for weeks.<br />	I expect there will be a row when my mother comes home and finds that I have gone. But frankly, my dear diary, I don’t give a damn. (p. 39)<br /><br />Any fans of British humor should appreciate this. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_461724427">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/461724427" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5921785-juliana-graham" class="left imgcol" title="Juliana Graham"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1312058766p2/5921785.jpg" alt="Juliana Graham" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/461724427?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 21, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5921785-juliana-graham" class="user" title="Juliana Graham">Juliana Graham</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7742547-the-secret-diary-of-adrian-mole-aged-13" title="Paperback 9780141046426" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer461724427">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3642890654362810925">This book has the honour of being the first one I read on a Kindle - I was persuaded to buy it by Amazon's sneaky advertising when you switch on the device; it was only 99p so it seemed rude not to! <br /><br />I had never read this book before but I know it was hugely popular when it came out (when I was a few years too young to read it) and it has also spawned many sequels, so there must be something to it. Overall, I read it quite quickly when I actually sat down with it (it wasn't my main book so took a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3642890654362810925">This book has the honour of being the first one I read on a Kindle - I was persuaded to buy it by Amazon's sneaky advertising when you switch on the device; it was only 99p so it seemed rude not to! <br /><br />I had never read this book before but I know it was hugely popular when it came out (when I was a few years too young to read it) and it has also spawned many sequels, so there must be something to it. Overall, I read it quite quickly when I actually sat down with it (it wasn't my main book so took a few weeks in total but probably not many hours). Some parts of it were amusing and I liked that I could really get a sense of time from the book - there was no doubt that this book was set in Thatcher's 80s. Adrian seems a very typical teenage boy, self obsessed and self conscious, convinced the world is out to get him. Not much of significance happens in the way of plot but that's to be expected - it's the diary of a 13 3/4 year old boy. The things that happen are of massive significance to him and that's all that matters!<br /><br />Whilst I did quite like the book, I don't feel like I care enough about the characters to read any more of the series. I'm glad I read it as everyone has heard of Adrian Mole - it was interesting to get a bit more of the picture. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3642890654362810925">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_704593042">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/704593042" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies" class="left imgcol" title="David Sarkies"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1445680853p2/5856247.jpg" alt="David Sarkies" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/704593042?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 04, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies" class="user" title="David Sarkies">David Sarkies</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1605077.The_Secret_Diary_of_Adrian_Mole_Aged_13_3_4" title="Perfect Paperback 9780749301385" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5856247-david-sarkies?shelf=comedy" class="actionLinkLite">comedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer704593042">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12924544084141775396"><strong>Inside the head of a teenager</strong><br />26 August 2013<br /><br /> I discovered this book because I had watched the TV series that was based on it and the reason that I watched the TV series was because when I was flicking through a computer magazine (when I was a kid) I found an add for 'The Secret Diary of Adrian Mole, aged 13 '. I guess that is how advertising is supposed to work because the only reason I read the book was because I had watched the TV series, and the only reason I watched the TV series was because</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12924544084141775396"><strong>Inside the head of a teenager</strong><br />26 August 2013<br /><br />	I discovered this book because I had watched the TV series that was based on it and the reason that I watched the TV series was because when I was flicking through a computer magazine (when I was a kid) I found an add for 'The Secret Diary of Adrian Mole, aged 13 ½'. I guess that is how advertising is supposed to work because the only reason I read the book was because I had watched the TV series, and the only reason I watched the TV series was because somebody had written an adventure game based on it and I like adventure games (though I didn't actually buy the book – I borrowed from the library). Come to think of it I went through the same process with regards to <a title="The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy (Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy, #1) by Douglas Adams" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11.The_Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy__Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy___1_">The Hitch-Hikers Guide to the Galaxy</a> (and I watched the show to see if I could get any hints for the game – I didn't). Though for some reason I think that the reason the computer game was written was so that Sue Townsend could cash in on the popularity of her books rather than sell more books (and since I borrowed the book from the library, I didn't actually buy it, so in the end she didn't sell more books, or at least sell another one to me).<br /><br />	The story is written in the form of diary entries (which is not actually all that original since Bram Stoker did something along those lines about a hundred years before, though his diary entries were by multiple people and also included newspaper clippings) as a young teenager travels the road of high school (not sure what it is called in England, but here in Australia it is high school). During this year he gets his first girlfriend, struggles with his O levels (whatever that is, though I suspect it is some form of standardised testing, though we didn't have them in Australia), and I believe he watches his parents get divorced.<br /><br />	I guess this is one of those books where we get to see inside the head of a teenager and are meant to realise that he goes through the same struggles as we all do. He deals with puberty, but also shows himself to be a bit of a geek by reading <a title="Peer Gynt  by Henrik Ibsen" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/279221.Peer_Gynt_">Peer Gynt</a> (nothing wrong with that, I quite liked Peer Gynt). In fact, he sets himself a goal to read Peer Gynt.<br /><br />	I wonder if this book is actually a more modern version of Peer Gynt. I don't think so because Adrian Mole does not go through the turmoil that Peer Gynt goes through, and we are only privy to Mole's teenage years, not his whole life, as is the case with Peer Gynt. I also do not believe that Mole earns the entire enmity of the town in which he lives by getting drunk at a wedding, running off with the bride, and then dumping her on some high mountain. However, one thing that we can consider is that Adrian Mole does seem to live in a dream world similar to Peer Gynt.<br /><br />	Could this book be a handbook on surviving puberty? Maybe, maybe not. It is clearly targeted towards those of Adrian's age, though I suspect much has changed in society since the days in which this book was popular. However, despite all of the changes in our society (especially the interconnectedness we now have with mobile phones and the Internet) there are still many things that are the same. However, I am unsure whether this is supposed to be a guidebook because everybody's experience of puberty is different. Still, it was a fun book to read, and in a way I did relate to Adrian Mole, and it did not matter that he was in England and I was in Australia, high school culture, somehow, seemed to be much the same.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12924544084141775396">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18307549034031773052">Now this story is probably one of the funniest I’ve read so far. Written by Sue Townsend it hits the country with its realism and the silliness of Adrian Mole himself.<br />It starts with his New Year to-do list which is an absolute killer all by itself. And then the reader slowly reads through the days of Adrian’s life and laughs him or herself silly just because of his weird ways of explaining things to himself.<br />Finally falls in love with a girl from his class and goes through the painful experience</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18307549034031773052">Now this story is probably one of the funniest I’ve read so far. Written by Sue Townsend it hits the country with its realism and the silliness of Adrian Mole himself.<br />It starts with his New Year to-do list which is an absolute killer all by itself. And then the reader slowly reads through the days of Adrian’s life and laughs him or herself silly just because of his weird ways of explaining things to himself.<br />Finally falls in love with a girl from his class and goes through the painful experience of watching her switch boyfriends.<br />Finally Pandora decides to go out with Adrian and the get on pretty well.<br />So the story goes on again, and the next stop is when Pandora goes to Tunisia for the holiday. Adrian is devastated and digested when Pandora gives all her money to a beggar instead of buying him a present.<br />After a week of reverse-charge calls to England from Pandora Adrian goes to the train station to meet her, but, gets onto the wrong platform.<br />Soon enough after that Adrian decides to go to Scotland with his mum and her lover Mr. Lucas. Finds it really boring and complains all the time.<br />When he comes back to England he goes back to school again. And with that, back to all the trouble.<br />So if you’re reading my review to decide whether to buy this book, my advice is to get it and not regret it.<br /></span>

      <a href="/user/show/1353392-emily" class="user" title="Emily">Emily</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer150286563">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10794388236237349864">Adrian Mole, precocious British teenager, self-professed intellectual, and diarist tells us of his trials and tribulations during the last part of his 13th and all of his 14th year. His musings are funny, sweet, and ultimately poignant. In this first edition of the series, we follow him through his decision to become an intellectual, his parents separation and reunification, and his tumultuous first love affair with one Pandora Braithwaite (herself precocious, radical and somewhat fickle.)<br />Upon m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10794388236237349864">Adrian Mole, precocious British teenager, self-professed intellectual, and diarist tells us of his trials and tribulations during the last part of his 13th and all of his 14th year. His musings are funny, sweet, and ultimately poignant. In this first edition of the series, we follow him through his decision to become an intellectual, his parents separation and reunification, and his tumultuous first love affair with one Pandora Braithwaite (herself precocious, radical and somewhat fickle.)<br />Upon my second reading of this book, I was pleased that I was not any less enchanted by Adrian as when I first became acquainted with him during my freshman year of college. Adrian is such a real and believable character that it's hard to believe he sprung from the mind of a middle-aged woman, who herself has never, presumably, been a 13 and 3/4 year old boy. Of course, neither have I. I am also not British, and not well-acquainted with early 1980's Britain and know nothing of British politics. I often find it difficult to read literature from countries I have not visited or studied extensively, but the colloquialisms herein are not as mystifying or unable to be understood from context in this work as others I have read.<br />I would recommend this book to any American Anglophile or any young adult who would in any way identify with the engaging character of Adrian Mole. </span>

      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pSgc19JuAMaX5V1HQdAglTV0wDZ+a5eVNarLC+e9oM7A/CMEILwUPBs9Kfw/scYnfIMDLze20D9fo86ZKyhWiw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Qns5RynwgS+riuj1k3X47gzZigzCvWl9TpX9+h/wFcMnrwaU2yKV1SdSnE7tFB5cRS5JFYtgLtcknPho02Xjhg==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

Ahead of him at the Polytechnic stretch years of trying to thump literature into the heads of plasterers, joiners, butchers and the like. And things are no better at home where his massive wife, Eva, is given to boundless and unpredictable fits of enthusiasm -for transcendental meditation, yoga or the trampoline. But if Wilt can do nothing about his job, he can do something about his wife, in imagination at least, and his fantasies grow daily more murderous and more concrete. After a peculiarly nasty experience at a party thrown by particularly nasty Americans, Wilt finds himself in several embarrassing positions: Eva stalks out in stratospheric dudgeon, and Wilt, under the inspiration of gin, puts one of his more vindictive fantasies into effect. But suspicions are instantly aroused and Wilt rapidly achieves an unenviable notoriety in the role of The Man Helping Police With Their Enquiries. Or is he exactly helping? Wilt\'s problem -although he\'s on the other side of the fence -is the same as Inspector Flint\'s: where is Eva Wilt? But Wilt begins to flourish in the heat of the investigation, and as the police stoke the flames of circumstantial evidence, Wilt deploys all his powers to show that the Law can\'t tell a Missing     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/28707.Sue_Townsend">About Sue Townsend</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/28707.Sue_Townsend"><img alt="28707" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1399722415p2/28707.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer17610546121500507569"><em>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces">See this thread for more information</a>.</em><br /><br />Susan Lillian "Sue" Townsend is a British novelist, best known as the author of the Adrian Mole series of books. Her writing tends to combine comedy with social commentary, though she has written purely dramatic works as well. She suffered from diabetes for many years, as a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17610546121500507569"><em>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces">See this thread for more information</a>.</em><br /><br />Susan Lillian "Sue" Townsend is a British novelist, best known as the author of the Adrian Mole series of books. Her writing tends to combine comedy with social commentary, though she has written purely dramatic works as well. She suffered from diabetes for many years, as a result of which she was registered blind in 2001, and has woven this theme into her work.</span>
